Former executive vice-president of Pixar, <a href="/wiki/John_Lasseter" title="John Lasseter">John Lasseter</a>, became <a href="/wiki/Chief_creative_officer" title="Chief creative officer">chief creative officer</a> of <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios" title="Walt Disney Animation Studios">Walt Disney Animation Studios</a>, its division <a href="/wiki/Disneytoon_Studios" title="Disneytoon Studios">Disneytoon Studios</a>, and Pixar Animation Studios, as well as assuming the role of principal creative advisor at <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Imagineering" title="Walt Disney Imagineering">Walt Disney Imagineering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PixarDisneySubsidiary_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PixarDisneySubsidiary-61">[49]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2006, Disney acquired the rights to <a href="/wiki/Oswald_the_Lucky_Rabbit" title="Oswald the Lucky Rabbit">Oswald the Lucky Rabbit</a> from <a href="/wiki/NBC_Universal" class="mw-redirect" title="NBC Universal">NBC Universal</a> (including the character's intellectual property and the 27 Oswald cartoons produced by Walt Disney) as part of an exchange of minor assets. In return, Disney released sportscaster <a href="/wiki/Al_Michaels" title="Al Michaels">Al Michaels</a> from his contracts with <a href="/wiki/ABC_Sports" class="mw-redirect" title="ABC Sports">ABC Sports</a> and ESPN, so he could join <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports" title="NBC Sports">NBC Sports</a> and his long-time partner <a href="/wiki/John_Madden" title="John Madden">John Madden</a> for NBC's new <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> <i><a href="/wiki/NBC_Sunday_Night_Football" title="NBC Sunday Night Football">Sunday Night Football</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[50]</a></sup> In April 2007, the Muppets Holding Company was moved from Disney Consumer Products to the <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a> division and renamed <a href="/wiki/The_Muppets_Studio" title="The Muppets Studio">The Muppets Studio</a>, as part of efforts to re-launch the division.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Muppets_2004_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muppets_2004-55">[45]</a></sup> In February 2007, the company was accused of human rights violations regarding the working conditions in factories that produce their merchandise.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[53]</a></sup> On August 31, 2009, Disney announced a deal to acquire <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel Entertainment</a> for $4.24 billion, in a deal completed on December 31, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[55]</a></sup></p><p>Director Emeritus Roy E. Disney died of <a href="/wiki/Stomach_cancer" title="Stomach cancer">stomach cancer</a> on December 16, 2009. At the time of his death, he owned roughly 1% of all of Disney which amounted to 16 million shares. He was the last member of the <a href="/wiki/Disney_family" title="Disney family">Disney family</a> to be actively involved in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[56]</a></sup> In October 2009, Disney Channel president <a href="/wiki/Rich_Ross" title="Rich Ross">Rich Ross</a>, hired by Iger, replaced <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cook" title="Dick Cook">Dick Cook</a> as chairman of the company and, in November, began restructuring the company to focus more on family friendly products. Later in January 2010, Disney decided to shut down Miramax after downsizing Touchstone, but one month later, they instead began selling the Miramax brand and its 700-title film library to <a href="/wiki/Filmyard_Holdings" title="Filmyard Holdings">Filmyard Holdings</a>. In March, <a href="/wiki/ImageMovers_Digital" class="mw-redirect" title="ImageMovers Digital">ImageMovers Digital</a>, which Disney had established as a joint venture studio with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Zemeckis" title="Robert Zemeckis">Robert Zemeckis</a> in 2007, was shut down. In April 2010, <a href="/wiki/Lyric_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyric Street">Lyric Street</a>, Disney's country music label in Nashville, was shut down. The following month, <a href="/wiki/Haim_Saban" title="Haim Saban">Haim Saban</a> reacquired the <i><a href="/wiki/Power_Rangers" title="Power Rangers">Power Rangers</a></i> franchise, including its 700-episode library.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[57]</a></sup> In September 2012, Saban reacquired the <i><a href="/wiki/Digimon" title="Digimon">Digimon</a></i> franchise, which, like <i>Power Rangers</i>, was part of the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Kids" title="Fox Kids">Fox Kids</a> library that Disney acquired in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[58]</a></sup> In January 2011, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Interactive_Studios" title="Disney Interactive Studios">Disney Interactive Studios</a> was downsized.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[59]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2011, Disney broke ground on <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Disney_Resort" title="Shanghai Disney Resort">Shanghai Disney Resort</a>. Costing $4.4 billion, the resort opened on June 16, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[60]</a></sup> Later, in August 2011, Bob Iger stated on a conference call that after the success of the <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel</a> purchases, he and the Walt Disney Company are looking to "buy either new characters or businesses that are capable of creating great characters and great stories."<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[61]</a></sup> Later, in early February 2012, Disney completed its acquisition of <a href="/wiki/UTV_Software_Communications" title="UTV Software Communications">UTV Software Communications</a>, expanding their market further into India and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[62]</a></sup> On October 30, 2012, Disney announced plans to acquire <a href="/wiki/Lucasfilm" title="Lucasfilm">Lucasfilm</a> in a deal valued at $4.05 billion. Disney announced an intent to leverage the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> franchise across its divisions, and planned to produce a <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">seventh installment</a> in the main film franchise for release in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[64]</a></sup> The sale was completed on December 21, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[65]</a></sup> On March 24, 2014, Disney acquired <a href="/wiki/Maker_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Maker Studios">Maker Studios</a>, an active <a href="/wiki/Multi-channel_network" title="Multi-channel network">multi-channel network</a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>, for $500 million.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[66]</a></sup> The company was later turned into a new venture called Disney Digital Network in May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[67]</a></sup></p><p>On February 5, 2015, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Staggs" title="Thomas O. Staggs">Tom Staggs</a> had been promoted to <a href="/wiki/Chief_operating_officer" title="Chief operating officer">COO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Staggs_COO_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Staggs_COO-80">[68]</a></sup> On April 4, 2016, Disney announced that Staggs and the company had mutually agreed to part ways, effective May 2016, ending his 26-year career with the company.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-Mutual_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-Mutual-81">[69]</a></sup> In August 2016, Disney acquired a 33% stake in <a href="/wiki/BAMTech" class="mw-redirect" title="BAMTech">BAMTech</a>, a streaming media provider spun out from <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>'s <a href="/wiki/MLB_Advanced_Media" title="MLB Advanced Media">media division</a>. The company announced plans to eventually use its infrastructure for an <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> <a href="/wiki/Over-the-top_content" class="mw-redirect" title="Over-the-top content">over-the-top</a> service.<sup id="cite_ref-variety-disneybam_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety-disneybam-82">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[71]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2016, Disney considered purchasing the American online <a href="/wiki/News" title="News">news</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_service" title="Social networking service">social networking</a> service <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[73]</a></sup> but they dropped out partly due to concerns over abuse and harassment on the service.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[76]</a></sup></p><p>On March 23, 2017, Disney announced that Iger had agreed to a one-year extension of his term as CEO through July 2, 2019, and had agreed to remain with the company as a consultant for three years after stepping down.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[78]</a></sup> In August 2017, Disney announced that it had exercised an option to increase its stake in BAMTech to 75%, and would launch a subscription <a href="/wiki/Video-on-demand" class="mw-redirect" title="Video-on-demand">video-on-demand</a> <a href="/wiki/Disney_streaming_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney streaming service">service</a> featuring its entertainment content in 2019, which will replace <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> as the subscription VOD rights holder of all Disney theatrical film releases.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-variety-disneymaj_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety-disneymaj-92">[80]</a></sup> In November 2017, Lasseter announced that he was taking a six-month leave of absence from Pixar and Disney Animation after acknowledging "missteps" in his behavior with employees in a memo to staff. According to various news outlets, Lasseter had a history of alleged sexual misconduct towards employees.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Foxstudiosentrance.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Foxstudiosentrance.jpg/220px-Foxstudiosentrance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2262" data-file-height="1659"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 161px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Foxstudiosentrance.jpg/220px-Foxstudiosentrance.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="161" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Foxstudiosentrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The entrance to Fox Studios lot.</div></div></div>
<p>In November 2017, it was reported by <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a> that Disney had been in negotiations to <a href="/wiki/Acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney" title="Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney">acquire</a> <a href="/wiki/21st_Century_Fox" title="21st Century Fox">21st Century Fox</a>. The negotiations had reportedly resumed around Disney acquiring several of Fox's key media assets. Rumors of a nearing deal continued on December 5, 2017, with additional reports suggesting that the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Networks" title="Fox Sports Networks">FSN</a> <a href="/wiki/Regional_sports_network" title="Regional sports network">regional sports networks</a> would be included in the resulting new company (assets that would likely be aligned with Disney's <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> division).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[86]</a></sup> On December 14, Disney agreed to acquire most assets from 21st Century Fox, including 20th Century Fox, for $52.4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[87]</a></sup> The merger included many of Fox's entertainment assets—including filmed entertainment, cable entertainment, and direct broadcast satellite divisions in the UK, Europe, and Asia<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[88]</a></sup>—but excluded divisions such as the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox Broadcasting Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Television_Stations" title="Fox Television Stations">Fox Television Stations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox News Channel">Fox News Channel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Business_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox Business Network">Fox Business Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_(United_States)" title="Fox Sports (United States)">Fox Sports</a> <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_1" title="Fox Sports 1">1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_2" title="Fox Sports 2">2</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Network" title="Big Ten Network">Big Ten Network</a>, all of which were to be spun off into an independent company before the merger was complete (which eventually named <a href="/wiki/Fox_Corporation" title="Fox Corporation">Fox Corporation</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Walt-Disney-Company-Dec-2017-8-K_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walt-Disney-Company-Dec-2017-8-K-101">[89]</a></sup> The following June, after a counter offer from Comcast worth $65 billion, Disney increased its offer to $71.3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyFoxBidIncrease_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyFoxBidIncrease-102">[90]</a></sup> The transaction officially closed on March 20, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[92]</a></sup></p><p>Beginning in March 2018, a strategic reorganization of the company saw the creation of two business segments, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Parks,_Experiences_and_Products" title="Disney Parks, Experiences and Products">Disney Parks, Experiences and Products</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Direct-to-Consumer_%26_International" title="Walt Disney Direct-to-Consumer &amp; International">Direct-to-Consumer &amp; International</a>. Parks &amp; Consumer Products was primarily a merger of Parks &amp; Resorts and Consumer Products &amp; Interactive Media. While Direct-to-Consumer &amp; International took over for Disney International and global sales, distribution and streaming units from Disney-ABC TV Group and Studios Entertainment plus Disney Digital Network.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[93]</a></sup> Given that CEO Iger described it as "strategically positioning our businesses for the future", <i>The New York Times</i> considered the reorganization done in expectation of the 21st Century Fox purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[94]</a></sup></p><p>On February 25, 2020, Disney named <a href="/wiki/Bob_Chapek" title="Bob Chapek">Bob Chapek</a> as CEO to succeed Iger, effective immediately. Iger will serve as the Executive Chairman during the transition period through 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[95]</a></sup> In April 2020, Iger reasserted active control of the company, taking back CEO duties to help the company through the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic" title="2019–20 coronavirus pandemic">2019–20 coronavirus pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[96]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Company_units">Company units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Walt_Disney_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Company units" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="List of assets owned by The Walt Disney Company">List of assets owned by The Walt Disney Company</a>.</div>
<p>The Walt Disney Company operates four primary business units, which it calls "business segments": <b>Studio Entertainment</b>, <b>Media Networks</b>, <b>Direct-to-Consumer &amp; International,</b> and <b>Parks, Experiences &amp; Products,</b> which includes the company's <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Parks_and_Resorts" class="mw-redirect" title="Walt Disney Parks and Resorts">theme parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Cruise_Line" title="Disney Cruise Line">cruise line</a>, travel-related assets, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Consumer_Products_and_Interactive_Media" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney Consumer Products and Interactive Media">consumer products</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disney_Publishing_Worldwide" title="Disney Publishing Worldwide">publishing divisions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[97]</a></sup> Studio Entertainment includes the company's primary business unit, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">The Walt Disney Studios</a>, which includes its film, music recording label, and theatrical divisions. Media Networks includes <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Television" title="Walt Disney Television">Walt Disney Television</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Inc." title="ESPN Inc.">ESPN Inc.</a>, and consists of the company's broadcast, cable, radio and publishing and digital businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-Buying_in_on_the_Disney_dream_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buying_in_on_the_Disney_dream-110">[98]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Direct-to-Consumer_%26_International" title="Walt Disney Direct-to-Consumer &amp; International">direct-to-consumer and international</a> division includes digital subscription streaming services and international holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-Buying_in_on_the_Disney_dream_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buying_in_on_the_Disney_dream-110">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel Entertainment</a> is also a direct CEO reporting business, while its financial results are primarily divided between the Studio Entertainment and Consumer Products segments.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[100]</a></sup></p><p>The company's main entertainment holdings include <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Music_Group" title="Disney Music Group">Disney Music Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Theatrical_Group" title="Disney Theatrical Group">Disney Theatrical Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Television" title="Walt Disney Television">Walt Disney Television</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Disney" title="Radio Disney">Radio Disney</a>, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, <a href="/wiki/FX_(TV_channel)#FX_Networks" title="FX (TV channel)">FX Networks</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Partners" title="National Geographic Partners">National Geographic Partners</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Interactive" title="Disney Interactive">Disney Interactive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Consumer_Products" title="Disney Consumer Products">Disney Consumer Products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a>, <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Studios" title="20th Century Studios">20th Century Studios</a>, <a href="/wiki/20th_Television" title="20th Television">20th Television</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_Sky_Studios" title="Blue Sky Studios">Blue Sky Studios</a>, <a href="/wiki/UTV_Software_Communications" title="UTV Software Communications">UTV Software Communications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Star_India" title="Star India">Star India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucasfilm" title="Lucasfilm">Lucasfilm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Disney_Digital_Network" title="Disney Digital Network">Disney Digital Network</a>. The company's resorts and diversified related holdings include <a href="/wiki/Disney_Parks,_Experiences_and_Products" title="Disney Parks, Experiences and Products">Disney Parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World" title="Walt Disney World">Walt Disney World</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Resort" title="Disneyland Resort">Disneyland Resort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Disney_Resort" title="Tokyo Disney Resort">Tokyo Disney Resort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Paris" title="Disneyland Paris">Disneyland Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Disneyland_Resort" title="Hong Kong Disneyland Resort">Hong Kong Disneyland Resort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Disney_Resort" title="Shanghai Disney Resort">Shanghai Disney Resort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Vacation_Club" title="Disney Vacation Club">Disney Vacation Club</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Cruise_Line" title="Disney Cruise Line">Disney Cruise Line</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Adventures_by_Disney" title="Adventures by Disney">Adventures by Disney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[101]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_management">Executive management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Walt_Disney_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Executive management" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_management_of_The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="List of management of The Walt Disney Company">List of management of The Walt Disney Company</a>.</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r891159353">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .multicol-float{width:auto!important}}.mw-parser-output .multicol-float{width:30em}</style><div class="multicol-float" style="clear:none;float:left;">
<dl><dt>Chairmen</dt></dl><p>Walt Disney stepped down as chairman in 1960 to focus more on the creative aspects of the company, becoming the "executive producer in charge of all production."<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[102]</a></sup><br>
After a four-year vacancy, Roy O. Disney became chairman.
</p>

<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references"><li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although Disney released a PG-rated film, <i><a href="/wiki/Take_Down_(1979_film)" title="Take Down (1979 film)">Take Down</a></i>, prior to the release of <i>The Black Hole</i>, they did not make the film; it was a pickup from independent producers.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references"><li id="cite_note-auto-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-auto_116-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_116-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Also named Films and Film Entertainment</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-CC-117"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-CC_117-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CC_117-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CC_117-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CC_117-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Merged into Creative Content in 1996, merged into Consumer Products and Interactive Media in 2016, which merged with Parks &amp; Resorts in 2018</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-WDIG-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-WDIG_118-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WDIG_118-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Internet_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Walt Disney Internet Group">Walt Disney Internet Group</a>, from 1997 to 2000, next merged with <a href="/wiki/Disney_Media_Networks" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney Media Networks">Disney Media Networks</a>, merged into Consumer Products and Interactive Media in 2016, which merged with Parks &amp; Resorts in 2018</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-DPR-120"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-DPR_120-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DPR_120-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Called Walt Disney Attractions (1989-2000) Walt Disney Parks and Resorts (2000-2005) Disney Destinations (2005-2008) Walt Disney Parks and Resorts Worldwide (2008-2018)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-auto1-121"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-auto1_121-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto1_121-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto1_121-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Broadcasting from 1994 to 1996</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-MVL-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-MVL_137-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-MVL_137-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">first year with Marvel Entertainment as part of results</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-148"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-148">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Not linked to WDIG, Disney reported a $300M loss due to financial modification regarding real estate</span>
